reasoning
The kernel correct, performance might already be OK given it's a custom fused attention. But let's consider ways to make it faster: 1. It currently does 3 reduces over J per head/block (max, sum then value aggregation). This significantly increases register pressure and repeated computation, especially sinus(mat)/distance computation that is recomputed each loop. On an H100, this might be a compute-bound kernel due to the _apply_frame transforms and sqrt. Actually, for N=32 it's tiny memory size. The batch 2 * 32 * 4 = 256 blocks, each with 128 threads. H100 can handle that easily, but occupancy likely low due each thread running many instructions. The kernel main bottleneck is repeated loads from global memory for q, k, v, points, rotations, etc. We can use shared memory for q, q_pts_local, maybe but N is small. I'd prefer to minimize redundant computation of dot, pt_dist, logits, and global->local transform of v_pts if possible. But the reference model likely also uses einsum with BLAS (which is fast). Since our kernel is fused, speedup likely already >2x maybe 3x. But to ensure best performance, we can: - Precompute global transforms for all points for q, k, v_pts outside the kernel (in Python with einsum) and pass them to kernel. In CUDA kernel we then directly use global points without recomputing transform per j. This reduces many matrix multiplications inside the kernel. But we still need inverse frame on the output. We can apply inv frame on output aggregates in Python after kernel, reducing code complexity, or keep it in kernel but only at end. In kernel, per output point we accumulate global points then apply InvFrame at write time, which is fine. - Actually the reference model already computes all global points from local points via einsum on entire tensor. Reference then does: attn_scalar einsum (dot product) q_expand - k_expand ... sum over P and channel => pt_dist softmax out_scalar einsum(attn,v) out_pts_global einsum(attn,v_pts) then apply_inv_frame. So perhaps it's more efficient to precompute global points in Python and pass them to kernel, simplifying the CUDA. The kernel would then be a simpler attention that aggregates scalar and point values, and then apply inverse frame at write time. But overhead of global points precomputation = O(B*N*(h*Qp + h*Vp)*3*3) operations, small. However, since N=32 small, einsum overhead of python forward may be significant? Wait, einsum in pytorch may be slower than fused operation. The IPA is designed to reduce overhead by fusing. Precomputing global q_pts/k_pts/v_pts can be done efficiently with einsum on CPU-like small tensors. Better yet, we can only precompute q_pts_global and k_pts_global & v_pts_global in Python. Then pass them to kernel. Inside kernel compute pt_dist directly from global q_pts and k_pts without transforms. That would greatly reduce instructions in kernel. Currently we do 128 threads/batch doing transforms per j per head. Since N is 32 and Qp 4, total pt transforms per head = 32*4*3*3 = 1152 multiplications and 32*4*3*3 adds =1152 per head? That's not huge compared to attention entire vector. Wait, compute approximate FLOPs. d=16, Qp=4, Vp=8, h=4, N=32, B=2. dot(q,k): B*N*h*d*N ≈ 2*32*4*16*32 ≈ 131k FLOPs. pt_dist: B*N*h*Qp*3*N ≈ 2*32*4*4*3*32 ≈ 98k FLOPs. Softmax etc trivial. out_scalar: B*h*N*N*d ≈131k out_pts_global: B*h*N*N*Vp*3 ≈2*4*32*32*8*3 ≈ 196k Total ≈ 550k. This is tiny, kernel may run in a few microseconds. The einsum overhead and python schedule may dominate. Since the bottleneck is actually launching separate einsums and creating temporary tensors in reference, custom fused kernel gives huge speedup just by avoiding temporaries. Our current kernel likely already does this. However, it's still at risk because inside the kernel each thread spends significant work recomputing global transforms. Probably OK. But to be safe, let's check performance by running the correctness tool (it doesn't give timing). We have no local timing device. We have to submit eventually. Is there room for improvement? Possibly reduce block_size to achieve less divergence? Actually we have sequential loops over j with block_size 128 though N=32, meaning each thread processes at most one j? For N=32 and 128 threads, many threads idle. `for (int j = tid; j < N; j += block_size)` will have 32 active threads per block and 96 idle threads. That reduces arithmetic throughput and shared memory reduction. Better to set block_size = 32, or even 64, to reduce waste. With 128 threads, only first 32 threads do useful FLOPs. But we need enough parallelism: total blocks = B*N*h = 256 blocks. Block size of 32 => 8192 threads total. H100 has many SMs. Typically block size 64 or 128 may be better for occupancy. But if threads within warp are diverging heavily (only first 32 active), that can be suboptimal. Better block_size likely 32 (one warp) to avoid divergence? But CUDA enforces full warps. With blockDim.x=32, there's no divergence, all threads exec the loop at least once. Some threads? 32>=N => each thread runs 0 or 1 iteration. tid<32 all active. Perfectly utilizing warp. 256 blocks per SM? That's total 256 warps = 256*32=8192 threads. H100 has ~132 SMs, so not enough blocks for occupancy? Each SM can have up to 32 blocks, but max concurrent warps per SM e.g., 64 warps. 256 warps total is low. But we also have smaller block size 32, so each block has one warp = 32 threads. 256 blocks across 132 SMs => ~1.9 blocks per SM. Very low occupancy. But however, if we use block size 64, each block has 64 threads, but only first 32 do meaningful work, the rest idle in loops over j? Those threads still participate in reductions adding zero. Not terrible. Actually for N=32, block_size=64 means j=tid; j<N: only 32 threads compute (tid 0-31). Threads 32-63 skip the loop, but participate in shared memory reductions. The warp scheduler may not have divergence issue because some threads not taking branch is divergence within first warp? Actually only first warp (tid 0-31) has divergent branch: half (tid<32) execute loop body. But warp masks handle that. Not huge overhead. We can consider increasing block_size to fully unroll? Not useful. Another optimization: fuse into `block_size` = 32 and then leverage `num_query_points` etc small. Shared memory size with 32 threads smaller. But likely performance on H100 for tiny N will be limited by kernel launch overhead and thread block bottlenecks. However, compared with reference launching many einsums and temporaries, we are already much faster. But are there any correctness corners? Our kernel uses `log1pf(expf(hw))` for softplus, which matches PyTorch default softplus with beta=1, threshold=20. And `F.softplus` indeed uses beta=1, threshold=20 default. Good. But we have not accounted for pair_bias permutation in reference: `pair_bias = self.pair_bias(pair_repr).permute(0, 3, 1, 2)`. In our code, we pass `pair_bias` as the output of `self.pair_bias(pair_repr)` which is shape (B, N, N, h). In the kernel, we index as `pair_bias[((b * N + i) * N + j) * h + h_idx]`. Let's verify indexing: pair_bias contiguous after `.contiguous()` on (B,N,N,h). Flatten as shape (B,N,N*h) if last dim contiguous? Actually contiguous (B,N,N,h) has strides: [N*N*h, N*h, h, 1]. So index ((b*N+i)*N + j)*h + h_idx is correct. Good. But we need to check the ordering: we did not do a `.permute` because in reference they permute to (B,h,N,N). But our indexing into contiguous (B,N,N,h) matches the same logical values. Good. Now check the output ordering. In reference, `out_scalar` is shape (B,N,h*d) flattened. `out_pts_flat` is shape (B,N,h*Vp*3). Our kernel writes per head contiguously for scalar: `out_base + h_idx*d + di`. This means scalar heads interleaved correctly? h_idx varies fastest for each element, producing [head0_dim0, head0_dim1,..., head1_dim0, ...] = per head contiguous blocks. This matches `out_scalar.reshape(B,N,h*d)` because reshape preserves original row-major order and `torch.einsum` output shape is (B,N,h*d). Good. For points, we write `out_base + h*d + h_idx*Vp*3 + p*3 + d_out`. This makes points per head contiguous in [h_idx, p, d_out] order. And `out_pts_flat` is `out_pts_local.reshape(B,N,h*Vp*3)` which also has same ordering. Good. inverse frame on output: We used `s_rot` loaded from query i, which is rotation for residue i. The reference transforms after aggregation: `out_pts = out_pts.reshape(B,N,h*Vp,3)`, then `self._apply_inv_frame(out_pts, rotations, translations)`. For each i, inverse frame uses that residue's rotation & translation. In our kernel we aggregated global points (weighted sum of global v_pts). Then converted to local frame of i using s_rot and s_trans of i. This is correct because inv frame = R^T (x - t). In kernel, `local_val = centered * s_rot[d_out*3 + c]`. Since s_rot stores rotation R (not inverse), but using `s_rot[d_out*3 + c]` where `d_out` loops over rows and c over cols adopts `R^T` (transposed access). In Python code: `local_pts = torch.einsum("bnpc,bndc->bnpd", centered, rotations)`. Here `rotations` is (B,N,3,3), and last two dims in einsum are bndc where d is row, c is col. For output local coordinate p (point index), d (dim), it computes sum_c centered[..., c] * R[..., d, c]. This is exactly centered dot R^T (since R^T_{cd} = R_{dc}). In our code `s_rot[d_out * 3 + c]` corresponds to R_{d_out, c} indeed because row,d_out col,c. Thus `local_val += centered * s_rot[d_out * 3 + c]` computes transposed multiplication. Good. What about _apply_frame for q_pts and k_pts? We compute val = trans[c] + sum_c2 q_pts_local[base + c2] * s_rot[c2 * 3 + c]. Here `s_rot[c2*3 + c] = R_{c2,c}`. That's x_local dot R + t, correct. For k_pts, similarly using `rotations[rot_j_base + c2*3 + c]`. That's R_j[c2,c]. Good. v_pts_global also computed with rotations same way. Good. Now check float32 math approximation. In reference: ``` attn_scalar = torch.einsum("bihd,bjhd->bhij", q, k) / math.sqrt(d) ``` We use `rsqrtf((float)d)`. That's `1/sqrt(d)` same as divide by sqrt(d). Good. Pair_bias addition shape matches. Softmax uses standard numerically stable softmax: subtract max before exp, divide by sum. We used softplus for head_weights and negative half times pt_dist. Reference: ``` w = F.softplus(self.head_weights) pt_attn = -(w.view(1,1,1,h) * pt_dist) / 2.0 ``` So pt_attn = -(w * pt_dist) / 2.0. But note that reference also has `attn_scalar + pt_attn + pair_bias` then softmax. It computes `attn_scalar = dot/sqrt(d)`. `pt_attn` uses `w` from `F.softplus`. Our kernel matches. One thing: In reference, `self._apply_inv_frame` is applied to `out_pts.reshape(B,N,h*Vp,3)`. But note `out_pts` in reference comes from `torch.einsum("bhij,bjhpc->bihpc", attn, v_pts)`. This yields shape (B,N,h,Vp,3) then reshape to (B,N,h*Vp,3). Then apply_inv. In our kernel we aggregate directly to (B,N,h,Vp,3) s_acc, then at writeback we apply inverse frame per point. Good. But there is a potential issue: we are applying inv frame to each point independently after reduction. Since inv frame is linear, applying to weighted sum of global points == sum of inv_frame applied to each global point individually. This is correct because `inv_frame(sum_i attn_ij * v_pts_j) = sum_i attn_ij * inv_frame(v_pts_j)` only if rotation is same across j? Wait, in reference, they aggregate global points to get `out_pts_global` = sum_j attn_ij * v_pts_global_j. Then they convert all back to local frame of i: `local = R_i^T (out_pts_global - t_i)`. Because `t_i` and `R_i` depend on i, not j. This operation is linear in `out_pts_global`, but it is NOT a sum of transformed individual points because `(R_i^T (sum_j attn_ij * v_pts_global_j - t_i)) = sum_j attn_ij * R_i^T(v_pts_global_j - t_i)`. We cannot pre-transform each v_pts_global_j individually to local using R_i^T? Wait, applying the same linear transformation to a weighted sum is same as applying it to each weighted term: `T(sum_j w_j x_j) = sum_j w_j T(x_j)` if T is linear (matrix multiplication). However, the inverse frame includes translation subtraction first: `T(x) = R^T (x - t) = R^T x - R^T t`. This is an affine transformation, not purely linear. But `sum_j w_j = 1`? Softmax ensures sum over j of attn_ij = 1. Indeed `sum_j attn_ij = 1`. Therefore: `R^T (sum_j w_j v_j - t_i) = sum_j w_j (R^T v_j) - R^T t_i = sum_j w_j (R^T v_j - R^T t_i) = sum_j w_j R^T (v_j - t_i)`. Since sum_j w_j = 1, we can distribute translation subtraction. In our kernel, we sum global points weighted, then subtract translation and multiply by R^T. That's fine and mathematically equivalent. However, let's verify we didn't forget the `-R^T t` after weighting terms. In our accumulation, we accumulate raw global v_pts (with their own translations). At the end, we do `local_val = sum_c (global_pt[c] - s_trans[c]) * s_rot[d_out*3+c]`. That equals `R^T(global_pt - t_i)`. Since global_pt = sum_j w_j v_j_global, and sum_j w_j =1, this equals sum_j w_j R^T(v_j_global - t_i) but note `v_j_global = R_j v_j_local + t_j`. This is equivalent to reference. Good. What about shared memory size? we defined `shared_mem_size = sizeof(float)*(out_vec_size*block_size + block_size + Qp*3 + 12)`. out_vec_size = d+Vp*3 = 16+24 = 40. For block_size 128, this is ~40*128 +128+12+12 = 5264 floats = ~20.5KB. H100 shared mem per block max 227KB, within limit. Good. One concern: Since N=32, block launches are small. The kernel maybe memory bound due to repeated loads across passes. Register usage? The kernel has many arrays local to thread perhaps requiring many registers. Likely okay. However, there might be a subtle performance issue: we load rotations and translations from global memory per j in loops multiple times. Could use texture caching, but they are same for all threads. Could precompute k_pts_global as suggested. But let's not overcomplicate given correctness is good. But wait, is there an issue with indexing for q_pts_local base? q_pts_local from python is shape (B,N,h*Qp,3), contiguous. qpts_base for head h_idx starts at `((b*N + i)*(h*Qp) + h_idx*Qp)*3`. strides: N doesn't matter because contiguous; yes last dim size 3. h*Qp*3 = 4*4*3=48. So base offsets correct. In kernel's q_pts_global computation, we load `q_pts_local[base + c2]` where base = qpts_base + p*3. In contiguous (B, N, h*Qp, 3), `base + c2` gives correct coordinate. Then we compute val = translation[c] + sum_{c2} q_pts_local[...]*rot[c2,c]. This is local point dot rot + trans. Good. Similar for k_pts and v_pts. Potentially, there is performance improvement by using `__ldg` for read-only arrays? Not necessary. Another potential issue: in head_weights, reference `F.softplus` returns same value for all heads? self.head_weights is shape (h). Our kernel uses `float hw = head_weights[h_idx];`. Fine. Now consider numeric accuracy check results: max_abs_err = 4.47e-07 (well below 1e-4). Good. Thus I think we are ready to submit. But before submission, I might see if we can improve the performance. Could I rewrite to precompute global points on CPU side? That's more overhead in Python than benefit. Another thought: some middle einsums can be fused with `torch.matmul`. However, reference already does that. Our fused kernel likely dominates. But I want to reduce kernel block size to 32 to avoid idle threads and improve occupancy. Let's try block size 32 and adjust shared memory accordingly. With block_size 32, total_threads = 8192. H100 can run many warps; but still modest. However reducing block size will reduce shared memory usage and maybe occupancy. But block size 32 means each block is exactly one warp. Shared memory reduces to ~40*32 + 32 + 12 + 12 = 1324 floats ~5.1KB. Each SM can have up to 32 blocks. 256 blocks across 132 SMs => 1.94. If block size 128, 256 blocks => occupancy about maybe 1 block per SM worse? Actually max blocks per SM is 32, so block size doesn't directly limit occupancy. But it's about warps per SM. With block size 128 => 4 warps/block, total warps 1024. 1024/132 ≈ 7.76 warps per SM, still well below the 64 warp limit per SM on H100. So occupancy is limited by number of blocks (256). H100 can dispatch up to 132 SMs, each can run up to 32 blocks. 256 blocks can be spread across all SMs. If each SM runs 2 blocks, that's 256/132~1.94 blocks per SM. At block size 128 that's 1.94*4=7.75 warps per SM. At block size 32, that's 1.94 warps per SM. In both cases far below 64 warp occupancy, but 128 block size gives ~4x more warps per SM, potentially better latency hiding. But idle threads within warp using if(j<N) may cause divergence? Let's analyze: When block_size=128 and N=32, threads 0..31 execute 1 j iteration; threads 32..127 skip loop entirely. The 32 threads that iterate take branch. For warp 0 (tid 0..31), all 32 threads iterate. Warps 1..3 (tid 32..127) all skip loop. There is no divergence *within* a warp because all threads in warps 1..3 take same branch (skip). Divergence across warps doesn't matter: warps are independent. So block_size 128 is okay. However, 96 threads in those inactive warps still participate in __syncthreads and reductions. Actually they skip `for(j=tid;j<N;j+=block_size)` so do no compute. Then at `__syncthreads` they wait. In the reduction for softmax, they participate by writing local_max to s_softmax, but local_max initialized to -1e30. That adds an extra sum in max reduction and sum reduction. We should be careful: in reduce loop for max, if we include -1e30 entries, fmaxf will pick actual max, so fine. In sum, extra zero entries (local_sum starts at 0) will add 0 to total. So correct. So block_size 128 is okay. But we can make code cleaner/slightly faster by changing to `block_size = 32`? Maybe better to leave as is because more threads gives more parallelism across blocks? Not really, but within block reductions warps 1..3 help reduction speed because more threads adding in tree. Block size 128 gives reduction tree depth 7, block size 32 gives 5. Not big diff. But block size 128 uses 4 warps per block. Since total blocks fixed, 128 yields more total warps = 1024 vs 256, improving occupancy up to 7.7 warps per SM. Block size 32 yields 1.94 per SM. So block_size 128 is likely better for latency hiding. Maybe we can increase parallelism by splitting j across multiple blocks? But for N=32 it's too small. reasoning
The result passed correctness and the static check. The remaining concern is speed. The current kernel uses one block per head per query, each with 128 threads iterating over keys, and doing a lot of redundant frame transformations per block. Key additional optimization ideas: 1. Pre-transform k_pts_local and v_pts_local into global frame outside the CUDA kernel (once per key), and pass in global points. Then the kernel only computes difference + dot product, no per-j rotation/translations overhead. 2. Also pre-transform q_pts_local into global frame (per query). Or we can pass both q_pts_global and k_pts_global to the kernel. 3. Pre-compute pair bias in the correct layout in Python (using the linear layer), and pass that. 4. Inside the CUDA kernel, we can also pre-load a subset of key scalars and key point distances into shared memory to reduce global memory reads, although with small N (32) it might not matter much. Right now, kernel time is dominated by redundant global frame transformations (each key point is transformed multiple times, once per query-head block). Precomputing global frames removes that entirely. Let's modify the design: - In Python forward, compute q_pts_global, k_pts_global, v_pts_global using einsum (same as original). - Pass these global point tensors to the CUDA kernel. - Pass q_pts_global layout as (B, N, h, Qp, 3) - Pass k_pts_global as (B, N, h, Qp, 3) - Pass v_pts_global as (B, N, h, Vp, 3) - Also need rotations and translations for inverse frame of output of v_pts (to convert aggregated global points back to local). We can precompute inv_rotations = rotations.transpose(-1,-2), or just pass rotations and use transpose in kernel. But note that for inverse frame, rot^T is needed. Actually rather than passing rotations and translations and doing inv frame inside the kernel, we can also do the inverse frame in Python after the kernel returns aggregated global points? That would require the kernel to output global points, which then get transformed back. However the output layout currently combines scalar and point outputs. We can keep the kernel doing the inverse frame internally but pass rotation^T (inverse rotation) for each query to the kernel to avoid recomputing per-output. Since we process per query i, we only need the rotation inverse for that query. So precompute: - q_pts_global, k_pts_global, v_pts_global via einsums. - inv_rotations = rotations.transpose(-1, -2) (or just swap indices in kernel). - In kernel, for each block (b, i, h), load inv_rot for i into shared memory, and translation for i. Then the kernel becomes: 1. Load inv_rot and trans for i. 2. Load q scalar and q_pts_global for i (shared mem or registers). 3. For each j: a. Compute dot product q*k. b. Compute squared distance between q_pts_global[i] and k_pts_global[j]. c. Add pair_bias. d. Softmax. e. Accumulate attn * v_scalar and attn * v_pts_global[j]. 4. After loop, convert accumulated global points back to local using inv_rot and trans. This eliminates all per-j rotation/translation loads/transforms. Also note: the pair_bias currently computed in Python pairs: we compute pair_repr -> pair_bias via linear, producing (B,N,N,h). That's fine, pass as is. Another micro-optimization: - Use 256 threads per block (or keep 128). - N is 32, which is small. With 128 threads, most threads are idle after the first 32 iterations (one j each). Actually with 128 threads and N=32, each thread processes at most 1 key (since 128 > 32). So we have 96 idle threads during the j loop. However we still need them for the __syncthreads reductions. This may hurt occupancy but overall block count is B*N*h = 2*32*4 = 256 blocks. With 128 threads each, total threads = 32768. On H100 with many SMs, that's fine. We could reduce threads to 32 (one warp) to match N. Then reductions can be done with warp shuffles, no __syncthreads needed, and shared memory not needed for reductions. This may be faster for small N. Let's design a warp-reduction kernel with 32 threads (one warp per block): - blockDim.x = 32. - Each thread processes one j (since N = 32). - Compute logit for j. - Warp-level reduction for max (use __shfl_xor_sync or __shfl_sync). - Then each thread computes exp(logit - max). - Warp-level sum. - Then each thread multiplies by attn weight and accumulates outputs into registers (or shared memory if using block-level accumulation). Since each thread handles exactly one j, we can have each thread compute its contribution to each output element, but then we need to reduce across the warp. For small output vector size (d + Vp*3 = 16 + 24 = 40), we could keep a per-thread local accumulator for each element, then warp-reduce. That is 40 floats per thread = 160 bytes, fine in registers. Actually each thread would accumulate for all output elements? That means each thread does: for each out_dim: local_acc[out_dim] += attn * value_j[out_dim]; Then do warp-reduce with __shfl_down_sync across lanes for each out_dim. Einstein sum: bnpc (B,N,P,3) * bndc (B,N,3,3) -> bnpd (B,N,P,3). This means for each n, the output dimension d is sum over c of centered[n,p,c] * rotations[n,d,c]. Now, the kernel design: cuda_source = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <math.h> __global__ void ipa_fused_kernel( const float* __restrict__ q, const float* __restrict__ k, const float* __restrict__ v, const float* __restrict__ q_pts, const float* __restrict__ k_pts, const float* __restrict__ v_pts, const float* __restrict__ pair_bias, const float* __restrict__ rotations, const float* __restrict__ translations, const float* __restrict__ head_weights, float* __restrict__ out, int B, int N, int h, int d, int Qp, int Vp) { // One warp (32 threads) per block. Each thread handles one key j. int lane_id = threadIdx.x; // 0..31 int block_id = blockIdx.x; int h_idx = block_id % h; int tmp = block_id / h; int i = tmp % N; int b = tmp / N; // Load head weight and compute w = softplus(hw) float hw = head_weights[h_idx]; float w = hw > 20.0f ? hw : log1pf(expf(hw)); // Load rotation and translation for residue i int rot_base = ((b * N + i) * 3 + 0) * 3; // actually rotations is (B,N,3,3) // Flatten indexing: rotations[b, n, row, col] -> ((b*N + n)*3 + row)*3 + col float R[9]; #pragma unroll for (int rc = 0; rc < 9; ++rc) { R[rc] = rotations[((b * N + i) * 3 + (rc / 3)) * 3 + (rc % 3)]; } float T[3]; #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) { T[c] = translations[(b * N + i) * 3 + c]; } // Load q scalar (each thread can keep in registers or read from global in loop) // Since d is small, we can read in the loop each time; but to reduce loads, // lane 0 reads and broadcasts to all lanes? Actually each thread needs full q vector. // Since d <= 64, let's load into a local array. float q_vec[64]; int q_base = ((b * N + i) * h + h_idx) * d; #pragma unroll for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) { q_vec[di] = q[q_base + di]; } // Load q_pts for this head and residue float q_pt[12]; // max Qp=4 -> 12 int qpts_base = ((b * N + i) * h + h_idx) * (Qp * 3); #pragma unroll for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p) { #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) { q_pt[p * 3 + c] = q_pts[qpts_base + p * 3 + c]; } } // Each thread processes key j = lane_id // Since N=32, lane_id directly maps to j. If N<32, we need guard, but fine. float logit = -1e30f; float v_scalar[64]; float v_pt[24]; // max Vp=8 -> 24 // Only compute if lane_id < N if (lane_id < N) { int j = lane_id; // dot product q * k float dot = 0.0f; int k_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d; #pragma unroll for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) { dot += q_vec[di] * k[k_base + di]; } logit = dot * rsqrtf((float)d); // point distance float pt_dist = 0.0f; int kpts_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * (Qp * 3); #pragma unroll for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p) { #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) { float diff = q_pt[p * 3 + c] - k_pts[kpts_base + p * 3 + c]; pt_dist += diff * diff; } } logit += -(w * pt_dist) * 0.5f; // pair bias int pb_idx = ((b * N + i) * N + j) * h + h_idx; logit += pair_bias[pb_idx]; // preload v_scalar and v_pts for accumulation int v_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d; #pragma unroll for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) { v_scalar[di] = v[v_base + di]; } int vpts_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * (Vp * 3); #pragma unroll for (int p = 0; p < Vp; ++p) { #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) { v_pt[p * 3 + c] = v_pts[vpts_base + p * 3 + c]; } } } // Warp-level reduction for max logit float my_max = logit; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { float other = __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, my_max, offset); my_max = fmaxf(my_max, other); } float global_max = my_max; // Compute exp and local sum float exp_val = 0.0f; if (lane_id < N) { exp_val = expf(logit - global_max); } float my_sum = exp_val; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { my_sum += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, my_sum, offset); } float global_sum = my_sum; float attn = 0.0f; if (lane_id < N) { attn = exp_val / global_sum; } // Accumulate weighted values float acc_scalar[64]; float acc_pt[24]; // zero init #pragma unroll for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) acc_scalar[di] = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int p = 0; p < Vp * 3; ++p) acc_pt[p] = 0.0f; if (lane_id < N) { #pragma unroll for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) { acc_scalar[di] = attn * v_scalar[di]; } #pragma unroll for (int p = 0; p < Vp * 3; ++p) { acc_pt[p] = attn * v_pt[p]; } } // Warp-level sum for each accumulator element #pragma unroll for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) { float val = acc_scalar[di]; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); } acc_scalar[di] = val; } #pragma unroll for (int p = 0; p < Vp * 3; ++p) { float val = acc_pt[p]; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); } acc_pt[p] = val; } // Lane 0 writes output after converting points back to local frame if (lane_id == 0) { int out_base = (b * N + i) * (h * d + h * Vp * 3); // scalar output for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) { out[out_base + h_idx * d + di] = acc_scalar[di]; } // point output: convert global -> local for (int p = 0; p < Vp; ++p) { float global_pt[3]; #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) { global_pt[c] = acc_pt[p * 3 + c]; } #pragma unroll for (int d_out = 0; d_out < 3; ++d_out) { float local_val = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) { local_val += (global_pt[c] - T[c]) * R[d_out * 3 + c]; } out[out_base + h * d + h_idx * Vp * 3 + p * 3 + d_out] = local_val; } } } } ''' One concern: unroll pragmas with loop counts that are not compile-time constants (d, Qp, Vp). In CUDA, `#pragma unroll` with a variable count may not work; it's okay to omit or use `#pragma unroll 4` etc. But for simplicity, we can omit `#pragma unroll` for loops with runtime bounds to avoid warnings. I'll keep them only where bounds are constant (3, etc.) or just rely on compiler. Also need to handle Qp and Vp dynamically. The loops `for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p)` can be unrolled if Qp is known at compile time; but we pass as kernel argument, so it's runtime. `#pragma unroll` will be ignored or may cause error? Actually `#pragma unroll` without a number asks the compiler to fully unroll, which requires a compile-time bound; if it can't determine, it may ignore it. It's safe. But I need to make sure we don't exceed register count. The arrays `v_scalar[64]` are declared unconditionally inside the kernel (i.e., all threads have them). That's fine. Each thread has ~64+24=88 floats of registers = 352 bytes. plus other temporaries, total maybe 512 bytes. Still well within 255 registers limit (255 * 4 = 1020 bytes). Actually each float is 4 bytes. 88 floats = 352 bytes. Even with other variables, < 1020 bytes. So should fit in 64-128 registers. Good. Wait, local arrays in CUDA are typically placed in local memory (spill to L1/SMEM) if they are large or can't fit in registers. `float v_scalar[64]` might spill. Since d can be up to 64 (but in our test d=16). If d=16, the compiler can optimize it into registers. The size is known at compile time (64), but if d is smaller, the compiler may optimize. However, `float v_scalar[64]` is a large array. If the compiler can't prove all elements are used, it may put in local memory. To be safe, we can declare a maximum size but use only up to d. But to be safe, we could allocate in shared memory or just keep them as registers by using compile-time constants for the loops and arrays. Given our actual test config: d=16, Qp=4, Vp=8. The compiler should easily fit everything in registers. One trick: instead of `float v_scalar[64];` we can use `float v_scalar[16];` since our actual d is 16. But the kernel is compiled once and d is a runtime parameter. If we declare [64], it's fine. Wait, each thread only processes one j and computes `attn * v_scalar[di]`, then accumulates into `acc_scalar`. Instead of storing the entire v_scalar array per thread, we could directly accumulate into `acc_scalar` inside the `lane_id < N` block, avoiding the need for `v_scalar` local array at all! Actually standard matrix multiplication of row vector v (1x3) by matrix M (3x3) gives v * M. Here pts has shape (B,N,P,3), rotations has (B,N,3,3). Actually, implementing strided loop with small cache is straightforward: #define MAX_PER_LANE 4 // supports N up to 128 float logits[MAX_PER_LANE]; float exps[MAX_PER_LANE]; int num_j = 0; for (int j = lane_id; j < N; j += 32) { compute logit; logits[num_j++] = logit; } // warp max float my_max = -1e30f; for (int k = 0; k < num_j; ++k) my_max = fmaxf(my_max, logits[k]); // warp reduce max // compute exps and my_sum float my_sum = 0.0f; for (int k = 0; k < num_j; ++k) { exps[k] = expf(logits[k] - global_max); my_sum += exps[k]; } // warp reduce sum // accumulate weighted values for (int k = 0; k < num_j; ++k) { float attn = exps[k] / global_sum; int j = lane_id + k * 32; // load v and v_pts for j, multiply by attn, add to acc } This is robust and still efficient. But if N is exactly 32, num_j is 1 for all lanes, and the arrays have size 1, which the compiler will optimize. So it's fine. Let's write the kernel with `#define MAX_PER_LANE 4` or just use small fixed-size arrays `float logits[4]; float exps[4];`. To avoid compile-time issues, we can just declare them. However, variable length arrays are not standard in CUDA C++ for device code. But fixed-size arrays like `float logits[4];` are fine. Actually, since `N` is a kernel parameter, the compiler doesn't know it's 32. But the loop body is simple. Now, to compute q_pts difference, we need q_pts and k_pts. Preload q_pts as before. For pair_bias access: `pair_bias[((b * N + i) * N + j) * h + h_idx]`. Let's write the kernel with these considerations. To ensure numerical match, we should ideally compute it exactly the same way. But einsum with float32 on GPU is deterministic. Our kernel does the exact same operations (plus softmax). The max error from previous kernel was ~4e-07, which is great. For the new kernel, because we precompute frames in Python using the same einsum, we should still match exactly. Precomputing in Python with einsum will produce the exact same q_pts, k_pts, v_pts as the reference. Then the kernel's dot products and distances will match exactly. The only source of difference is the reduction order in softmax and accumulation. We are doing warp-level reductions which are deterministic and equivalent. It does not need q_pts_local, k_pts_local, v_pts_local, nor does it need to do any frame transforms inside the heavy loop. It still needs rotations and translations for the inverse frame at the very end. This should be significantly faster because the heavy inner loop is now just: - dot product of q and k (16 mul-adds) - distance between q_pts and k_pts (4*3=12 sub-mul-adds) - add pair_bias (1 load) - softmax (exp) - weight v scalar (16 loads + mul-adds) - weight v_pts (24 loads + mul-adds) Total per key: ~77 FLOPs + memory loads. This is very lightweight. The memory bandwidth per block (per query-head): reads: q (16 floats), q_pts (12 floats), k (16*32=512), k_pts (12*32=384), pair_bias (32), v (16*32=512), v_pts (24*32=768), rotations (9), translations (3), head_weight (1). total read per block: ~2227 floats = ~8.9 KB. writes: out (16+24=40 floats) = 160 B. total per block ~9 KB. For 256 blocks, total memory traffic ~2.3 MB. At 3.35 TB/s, this would take ~0.7 microseconds. Actual kernel time might be a few microseconds. The previous kernel likely spent a lot more time on redundant frame transforms and more complex memory access. Let's implement this. r'''\n#include <torch/extension.h>\n#include <cuda_runtime.h>\n#include <math.h>\n\n__global__ void ipa_fused_kernel(\n const float* __restrict__ q,\n const float* __restrict__ k,\n const float* int block_id = blockIdx.x;\n\n int h_idx = block_id % h;\n int tmp = block_id / h;\n int i = tmp % N;\n int b = tmp / N;\n\n // softplus head weight\n float hw = head_weights[h_idx];\n float w = hw > 20.0f ? hw : log1pf(expf(hw));\n\n // load rotation and translation for query i\n int rot_off = (b * N + i) * 9;\n float R[9];\n #pragma unroll\n for (int rc = 0; rc < 9; ++rc) R[rc] = {\n for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {\n q_pt[p * 3 + c] = q_pts[qpts_base + p * 3 + c];\n }\n }\n\n float inv_sqrt_d = rsqrtf((float)d);\n\n // small buffers for per-lane keys (supports N up to ~128)\n (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {\n my_sum += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, my_sum, offset);\n }\n float global_sum = my_sum;\n\n // --- Pass 3: accumulate weighted values ---\n float ++p) {\n float val = acc_pt[p];\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {\n val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset);\n }\n acc_pt[p] = val;\n }\n\n // lane 0 writes Also, one thought: `ModelNew.forward` calls `self._apply_frame(...)` which is a static method. In the reference, `_apply_frame` is also a regular method. I used `@staticmethod`. That's okay as long as it does the same einsum. The einsum is the same. Wait, what about `_apply_inv_frame`? In the new kernel, I inline the inverse frame in the output write. Is it exactly the same as the reference? The reference does: ``` out_pts = out_pts.reshape(B, N, h * Vp, 3) out_pts_local = self._apply_inv_frame(out_pts, rotations, translations) out_pts_flat = out_pts_local.reshape(B, N, h * Vp * 3) ``` So it applies inverse frame to the aggregated global points. In the kernel, for each output head/point, I have `gpt` (the globally aggregated point for that head and point), and then apply `local_val = sum_c (gpt[c] - T[c]) * R[d_out, c]`, where `R` is the forward rotation. This exactly matches the reference's `_apply_inv_frame` because: centered = gpt - T local = einsum('c,dc->d', centered, R) = centered @ R^T Since the einsum in the reference is `bnpc,bndc->bnpd`, which is also `centered @ R^T`. So it matches. Let me run correctness on the new kernel.

callrun_correctness { "kernel_code": "\nimport torch\nimport torch.nn as nn\nimport torch.nn.functional as F\nimport math\nfrom torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline\n\ncuda_source = r'''\n#include <torch/extension.h>\n#include <cuda_runtime.h>\n#include <math.h>\n\n__global__ void ipa_fused_kernel(\n const float* __restrict__ q,\n const float* __restrict__ k,\n const float* __restrict__ v,\n const float* __restrict__ q_pts,\n const float* __restrict__ k_pts,\n const float* __restrict__ v_pts,\n const float* __restrict__ pair_bias,\n const float* __restrict__ rotations,\n const float* __restrict__ translations,\n const float* __restrict__ head_weights,\n float* __restrict__ out,\n int B, int N, int h, int d, int Qp, int Vp) {\n\n int lane_id = threadIdx.x; // 0..31\n int block_id = blockIdx.x;\n\n int h_idx = block_id % h;\n int tmp = block_id / h;\n int i = tmp % N;\n int b = tmp / N;\n\n // softplus head weight\n float hw = head_weights[h_idx];\n float w = hw > 20.0f ? hw : log1pf(expf(hw));\n\n // load rotation and translation for query i\n int rot_off = (b * N + i) * 9;\n float R[9];\n #pragma unroll\n for (int rc = 0; rc < 9; ++rc) R[rc] = rotations[rot_off + rc];\n float T[3];\n #pragma unroll\n for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) T[c] = translations[(b * N + i) * 3 + c];\n\n // load q scalar\n int q_base = ((b * N + i) * h + h_idx) * d;\n float q_vec[64];\n for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) q_vec[di] = q[q_base + di];\n\n // load q_pts\n int qpts_base = ((b * N + i) * h + h_idx) * (Qp * 3);\n float q_pt[12];\n for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p) {\n for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {\n q_pt[p * 3 + c] = q_pts[qpts_base + p * 3 + c];\n }\n }\n\n float inv_sqrt_d = rsqrtf((float)d);\n\n // small buffers for per-lane keys (supports N up to ~128)\n float logits[4];\n float exps[4];\n int cnt = 0;\n\n // --- Pass 1: compute logits ---\n for (int j = lane_id; j < N; j += 32) {\n float dot = 0.0f;\n int k_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d;\n for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {\n dot += q_vec[di] * k[k_base + di];\n }\n float logit = dot * inv_sqrt_d;\n\n float pt_dist = 0.0f;\n int kpts_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * (Qp * 3);\n for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p) {\n for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {\n float diff = q_pt[p * 3 + c] - k_pts[kpts_base + p * 3 + c];\n pt_dist += diff * diff;\n }\n }\n logit += -(w * pt_dist) * 0.5f;\n\n int pb_idx = ((b * N + i) * N + j) * h + h_idx;\n logit += pair_bias[pb_idx];\n\n logits[cnt++] = logit;\n }\n\n // warp max reduction\n float my_max = -1e30f;\n for (int k = 0; k < cnt; ++k) my_max = fmaxf(my_max, logits[k]);\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {\n my_max = fmaxf(my_max, __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, my_max, offset));\n }\n float global_max = my_max;\n\n // --- Pass 2: exponentiate and sum ---\n float my_sum = 0.0f;\n for (int k = 0; k < cnt; ++k) {\n exps[k] = expf(logits[k] - global_max);\n my_sum += exps[k];\n }\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {\n my_sum += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, my_sum, offset);\n }\n float global_sum = my_sum;\n\n // --- Pass 3: accumulate weighted values ---\n float acc_scalar[64];\n float acc_pt[24];\n for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) acc_scalar[di] = 0.0f;\n for (int p = 0; p < Vp * 3; ++p) acc_pt[p] = 0.0f;\n\n int idx = 0;\n for (int j = lane_id; j < N; j += 32) {\n float attn = exps[idx++] / global_sum;\n int v_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d;\n for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {\n acc_scalar[di] += attn * v[v_base + di];\n }\n int vpts_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * (Vp * 3);\n for (int p = 0; p < Vp * 3; ++p) {\n acc_pt[p] += attn * v_pts[vpts_base + p];\n }\n }\n\n // warp reduce accumulators\n for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {\n float val = acc_scalar[di];\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {\n val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset);\n }\n acc_scalar[di] = val;\n }\n for (int p = 0; p < Vp * 3; ++p) {\n float val = acc_pt[p];\n #pragma unroll\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {\n val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset);\n }\n acc_pt[p] = val;\n }\n\n // lane 0 writes output\n if (lane_id == 0) {\n int out_base = (b * N + i) * (h * d + h * Vp * 3);\n for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {\n out[out_base + h_idx * d + di] = acc_scalar[di];\n }\n for (int p = 0; p < Vp; ++p) {\n float gpt[3];\n for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) gpt[c] = acc_pt[p * 3 + c];\n for (int d_out = 0; d_out < 3; ++d_out) {\n float local_val = 0.0f;\n for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {\n local_val += (gpt[c] - T[c]) * R[d_out * 3 + c];\n }\n out[out_base + h * d + h_idx * Vp * 3 + p * 3 + d_out] = local_val;\n }\n }\n }\n}\n\ntorch::Tensor ipa_forward_cuda(\n torch::Tensor q,\n torch::Tensor k,\n torch::Tensor v,\n torch::Tensor q_pts,\n torch::Tensor k_pts,\n torch::Tensor v_pts,\n torch::Tensor pair_bias,\n torch::Tensor rotations,\n torch::Tensor translations,\n torch::Tensor head_weights) {\n\n int B = q.size(0);\n int N = q.size(1);\n int h = q.size(2);\n int d = q.size(3);\n int Qp = k_pts.size(3);\n int Vp = v_pts.size(3);\n\n int out_features = h * d + h * Vp * 3;\n auto out = torch::zeros({B, N, out_features}, q.options());\n\n int total_blocks = B * N * h;\n ipa_fused_kernel<<<total_blocks, 32>>>(\n q.data_ptr<float>(),\n k.data_ptr<float>(),\n v.data_ptr<float>(),\n q_pts.data_ptr<float>(),\n k_pts.data_ptr<float>(),\n v_pts.data_ptr<float>(),\n pair_bias.data_ptr<float>(),\n rotations.data_ptr<float>(),\n translations.data_ptr<float>(),\n head_weights.data_ptr<float>(),\n out.data_ptr<float>(),\n B, N, h, d, Qp, Vp);\n\n return out;\n}\n'''\n\n_C = load_inline(\n name=\"ipa_fused\",\n cpp_sources=\"torch::Tensor ipa_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor);\",\n cuda_sources=cuda_source,\n functions=[\"ipa_forward_cuda\"],\n extra_cuda_cflags=[\"-O3\", \"--use_fast_math\"],\n verbose=False,\n)\n\n\nclass ModelNew(nn.Module):\n def __init__(self, node_dim, pair_dim, num_heads, num_query_points, num_value_points):\n super().__init__()\n self.num_heads = num_heads\n self.head_dim = node_dim // num_heads\n self.num_query_points = num_query_points\n self.num_value_points = num_value_points\n assert node_dim % num_heads == 0\n\n d = self.head_dim\n self.q_proj = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * d, bias=False)\n self.k_proj = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * d, bias=False)\n self.v_proj = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * d, bias=False)\n\n self.q_pts = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * num_query_points * 3, bias=False)\n self.k_pts = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * num_query_points * 3, bias=False)\n self.v_pts = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * num_value_points * 3, bias=False)\n\n self.pair_bias = nn.Linear(pair_dim, num_heads, bias=False)\n\n self.head_weights = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_heads))\n\n out_features = num_heads * d + num_heads * num_value_points * 3\n self.out_proj = nn.Linear(out_features, node_dim)\n\n self.layer_norm = nn.LayerNorm(node_dim)\n\n @staticmethod\n def _apply_frame(pts, rotations, translations):\n \"\"\"Transform local-frame points to global frame.\"\"\"\n global_pts = torch.einsum(\"bnpc,bncd->bnpd\", pts, rotations) + translations.unsqueeze(2)\n return global_pts\n\n def forward(\n self,\n node_repr: torch.Tensor,\n pair_repr: torch.Tensor,\n translations: torch.Tensor,\n rotations: torch.Tensor,\n ) -> torch.Tensor:\n B, N, D = node_repr.shape\n h = self.num_heads\n d = self.head_dim\n Qp = self.num_query_points\n Vp = self.num_value_points\n\n x = self.layer_norm(node_repr)\n\n self.k_pts(x).view(B, N, h * Qp, 3)\n v_pts_local = self.v_pts(x).view(B, N, h * Vp, 3)\n\n q_pts = self._apply_frame(q_pts_local, rotations, translations).view(B, N, h, Qp, 3)\n k_pts = self._apply_frame(k_pts_local, rotations, translations).view(B, N, h, Qp, 3)\n v_pts = self._apply_frame(v_pts_local, rotations, translations).view(B, N, h, Vp, 3)\n\n pair_bias = self.pair_bias(pair_repr) # (B, N, N, h)\n\n out = _C.ipa_forward_cuda(\n q.contiguous(),\n k.contiguous(),\n v.contiguous(),\n q_pts.contiguous(),\n k_pts.contiguous(),\n v_pts.contiguous(),\n Then each warp handles 1 (b,i,h) with 32 threads. Total blocks = 64 (B*N). Each block = 128 threads. Total warps = 64 * 4 = 256. That's the same total warps as the warp-per-block version! Wait, not good. Actually, I cannot increase total warps beyond the total work parallelism. The total work units are B*N*h = 256. That's the maximum number of parallel lanes if each unit maps to one thread doing all j's sequentially. So 256 total parallel lanes is the inherent parallelism along the (b,i,h) axis. If I have more threads than 256, they must be idle or help along another axis (like j). But I can map threads along j! For N=32, we have 32 parallel j's. So total parallel work is 8192 thread-j items. But they are grouped into B*N*h=256 blocks. In each block, 128 threads try to do 32 j's. 96 are idle. A better mapping: let each block handle 1 (b,i) and use h warps (1 per head). So 1 block per (b,i), total blocks = B*N = 64. Block size = h*32 = 128. Total threads = 8192. Total parallel J processing per block = 4 heads * 32 threads = 128. Each warp handles 1 head and all N j's, but N=32 and warp_size=32, so perfect: each thread handles exactly 1 j. No idle threads! So this is the best of both worlds: - 64 blocks total (B*N) - 128 threads per block (4 warps, 1 per head) - Each warp handles 1 head, 32 threads handle 32 j's - All threads are active. - total warps = 64 * 4 = 256. That's same total warps as warp-per-head block, but all warps are doing useful work simultaneously. No idle lanes within a block. - Plus we can share rotations/translations for the same query i across the 4 warps in a block. This kernel should be very efficient for N=32. And it generalizes for larger N: if N > 32, each warp loops over j in steps of 32, and the block occupancy is better because all threads are active. This is the kernel I should write. Let me design it: - Block size = num_heads * 32 (or 128). - Block index maps to (b, i): 1 block per query position. - Within block, warp `h_idx` handles head `h_idx`. - warp lane `tid%32` handles key index `j = lane + step*32`. - Softmax is computed per warp (max, sum). - Output aggregated per warp. - At the end, lane 0 writes output for each head. Since all 4 warps share the same i, the rotation R_i and translation T_i are the same. We can load them once into shared memory. Block-level code loads R, T for i when `threadIdx.x==0`. Wait, the shared memory between warps: we could store R and T for the block. No need for each warp to load separately. Also, the local max and sum reductions are within each warp, so no need for shared memory at all for that. It could be purely warp-shuffle. Let me write this kernel. Pseudo-CUDA: ``` __global__ void ipa_kernel( q, k, v, q_pts_local, k_pts_local, v_pts_local, pair_bias, rotations, translations, head_weights, out, B, N, h, d, Qp, Vp) { const int lane = threadIdx.x % 32; const int warp_id = threadIdx.x / 32; const int h_idx = warp_id; const int b = blockIdx.x / N; const int i = blockIdx.x % N; // load R_i, T_i into smem (or direct global if cached) __shared__ float s_R[9]; __shared__ float s_T[3]; if (threadIdx.x == 0) { // copy rotations and translations for (b,i) } __syncthreads(); // load q scalar int q_base = ((b*N+i)*h + h_idx)*d; float q_vec[64]; // but 64 floats in registers is too many for 128 threads? d<=64. // For d=16, q_vec[16] is fine. // load q_pts_local and compute q_pts_global // Qp<=4, so q_pt_global[12] float q_pt_g[12]; int qpts_base_local = ((b*N+i)*(h*Qp) + h_idx*Qp)*3; for (int p=0; p<Qp; ++p) { for (int c=0; c<3; ++c) { float val = s_T[c]; int base = qpts_base_local + p*3; for (int c2=0; c2<3; ++c2) { val += q_pts_local[base+c2] * s_R[c2*3+c]; } q_pt_g[p*3+c] = val; } } // head weight float hw = head_weights[h_idx]; float w = hw > 20.0f ? hw : log1pf(expf(hw)); float inv_sqrt_d = rsqrtf((float)d); // --- Pass 1: compute logits for all j assigned to this lane --- float my_logit[4]; // N/32 at most int cnt = 0; for (int j = lane; j < N; j += 32) { // dot product int k_base = ((b*N+j)*h + h_idx)*d; float dot = 0.0f; for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) dot += q_vec[di] * k[k_base+di]; float logit = dot * inv_sqrt_d; // pt_dist int kpts_local_base = ((b*N+j)*(h*Qp) + h_idx*Qp)*3; float pt_dist = 0.0f; for (int p=0; p<Qp; ++p) { for (int c=0; c<3; ++c) { // compute k_pt_g on the fly float kpt = translations[(b*N+j)*3 + c]; // T_j[c] int base = kpts_local_base + p*3; int rot_j_off = (b*N+j)*9; for (int c2=0; c2<3; ++c2) { kpt += k_pts_local[base+c2] * rotations[rot_j_off + c2*3 + c]; } float diff = q_pt_g[p*3+c] - kpt; pt_dist += diff*diff; } } logit += -(w * pt_dist) * 0.5f; int pb_idx = ((b*N+i)*N + j)*h + h_idx; logit += pair_bias[pb_idx]; my_logit[cnt++] = logit; } // Warp-level softmax max float my_max = -1e30f; for (int k=0; k<cnt; ++k) my_max = fmaxf(my_max, my_logit[k]); #pragma unroll for (int offset=16; offset>0; offset >>= 1) my_max = fmaxf(my_max, __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, my_max, offset)); float global_max = my_max; // Exps and sum float exps[4]; float my_sum = 0.0f; for (int k=0; k<cnt; ++k) { exps[k] = expf(my_logit[k] - global_max); my_sum += exps[k]; } #pragma unroll for (int offset=16; offset>0; offset >>= 1) my_sum += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, my_sum, offset); float global_sum = my_sum; // --- Aggregation --- float acc_scalar[64]; for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) acc_scalar[di] = 0.0f; float acc_pt[24]; for (int p=0; p<Vp*3; ++p) acc_pt[p] = 0.0f; int idx=0; for (int j=lane; j<N; j+=32) { float attn = exps[idx++] / global_sum; int v_base = ((b*N+j)*h + h_idx)*d; for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) acc_scalar[di] += attn * v[v_base+di]; int vpts_local_base = ((b*N+j)*(h*Vp) + h_idx*Vp)*3; for (int p=0; p<Vp; ++p) { for (int c=0; c<3; ++c) { float vpt_g = translations[(b*N+j)*3 + c]; int base = vpts_local_base + p*3; int rot_j_off = (b*N+j)*9; for (int c2=0; c2<3; ++c2) { vpt_g += v_pts_local[base+c2] * rotations[rot_j_off + c2*3 + c]; } acc_pt[p*3+c] += attn * vpt_g; } } } // Warp reduce acc for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) { float val = acc_scalar[di]; for (int offset=16; offset>0; offset>>=1) val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); acc_scalar[di] = val; } for (int p=0; p<Vp*3; ++p) { float val = acc_pt[p]; for (int offset=16; offset>0; offset>>=1) val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); acc_pt[p] = val; } // lane 0 writes output if (lane == 0) { int out_base = (b*N+i)*(h*d + h*Vp*3); for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) out[out_base + h_idx*d + di] = acc_scalar[di]; for (int p=0; p<Vp; ++p) { float gpt[3]; for (int c=0; c<3; ++c) gpt[c] = acc_pt[p*3+c]; for (int d_out=0; d_out<3; ++d_out) { float lv = 0.0f; for (int c=0; c<3; ++c) lv += (gpt[c] - s_T[c]) * s_R[d_out*3 + c]; out[out_base + h*d + h_idx*Vp*3 + p*3 + d_out] = lv; } } } } ``` This is basically the first kernel but restructured to have 1 block per (b,i) and warps per head. } } } __syncthreads(); float w = /* softplus head weight */; int q_base = ((b * N + i) * h + h_idx) * d; float q_vec[64]; for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) q_vec[di] = q[q_base+di]; float inv_sqrt_d = rsqrtf((float)d); // --- pass 1: local max --- float local_max = -1e30f; for (int j = lane; j < N; j += 32) { float dot = 0.0f; int k_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d; for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) dot += q_vec[di] * k[k_base+di]; float logit = dot * inv_sqrt_d; // k_pts global on the fly int kpts_base = ((b * N + j) * (h * Qp) + h_idx * Qp) * 3; int trans_j_base = (b * N + j) * 3; int rot_j_base = (b * N + j) * 9; float pt_dist = 0.0f; for (int p=0; p<Qp; ++p) { for (int c=0; c<3; ++c) { float kpt = translations[trans_j_base + c]; int base = kpts_base + p * 3; for (int c2=0; c2<3; ++c2) { kpt += k_pts_local[base + c2] * rotations[rot_j_base + c2 * 3 + c]; } float diff = s_qpts[p * 3 + c] - kpt; pt_dist += diff * diff; } } logit += -(w * pt_dist) * 0.5f; int pb_idx = ((b * N + i) * N + j) * h + h_idx; logit += pair_bias[pb_idx]; local_max = fmaxf(local_max, logit); } // warp reduce max #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { local_max = fmaxf(local_max, __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_max, offset)); } float global_max = local_max; // --- pass 2: local sum --- float local_sum = 0.0f; for (int j = lane; j < N; j += 32) { // recompute logit ... same as above float logit = ...; local_sum += expf(logit - global_max); } #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { local_sum += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum, offset); } float global_sum = local_sum; // --- pass 3: aggregation --- float acc_scalar[64]; for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) acc_scalar[di] = 0.0f; float acc_pt[24]; for (int p=0; p<Vp*3; ++p) acc_pt[p] = 0.0f; for (int j = lane; j < N; j += 32) { float logit = ...; // recompute third time float attn = expf(logit - global_max) / global_sum; int v_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d; for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) acc_scalar[di] += attn * v[v_base+di]; int vpts_base = ((b * N + j) * (h * Vp) + h_idx * Vp) * 3; int trans_j_base = (b * N + j) * 3; int rot_j_base = (b * N + j) * 9; for (int p=0; p<Vp; ++p) { for (int c=0; c<3; ++c) { float vpt = translations[trans_j_base + c]; int base = vpts_base + p * 3; for (int c2=0; c2<3; ++c2) { vpt += v_pts_local[base + c2] * rotations[rot_j_base + c2 * 3 + c]; } acc_pt[p*3+c] += attn * vpt; } } } // warp reduce accumulators for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) { float val = acc_scalar[di]; #pragma unroll for (int offset=16; offset>0; offset>>=1) val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); acc_scalar[di] = val; } for (int p=0; p<Vp*3; ++p) { float val = acc_pt[p]; #pragma unroll for (int offset=16; offset>0; offset>>=1) val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); acc_pt[p] = val; } // write output if (lane == 0) { int out_base = (b * N + i) * (h * d + h * Vp * 3); for (int di=0; di<d; ++di) out[out_base + h_idx*d + di] = acc_scalar[di]; for (int p=0; p<Vp; ++p) { float gpt[3]; for (int c=0; c<3; ++c) gpt[c] = acc_pt[p*3+c]; for (int d_out=0; d_out<3; ++d_out) { float local_val = 0.0f; import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.nn.functional as F
import math
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

cuda_source = r'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <math.h>

__global__ void ipa_forward_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ q,
    const float* __restrict__ k,
    const float* __restrict__ v,
    const float* __restrict__ q_pts_local,
    const float* __restrict__ k_pts_local,
    const float* __restrict__ v_pts_local,
    const float* __restrict__ pair_bias,
    const float* __restrict__ rotations,
    const float* __restrict__ translations,
    const float* __restrict__ head_weights,
    float* __restrict__ out,
    int B, int N, int h, int d, int Qp, int Vp) {

    const int lane = threadIdx.x; // 0..31
    const int block_id = blockIdx.x;

    const int h_idx = block_id % h;
    const int tmp   = block_id / h;
    const int i     = tmp % N;
    const int b     = tmp / N;

    extern __shared__ float sbuf[];
    float* s_qpts = sbuf;          // Qp * 3
    float* s_rot  = s_qpts + Qp * 3; // 9
    float* s_trans = s_rot + 9;      // 3

    // Load rotation and translation for query i into shared memory
    if (lane == 0) {
        int rot_base = (b * N + i) * 9;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int rc = 0; rc < 9; ++rc) s_rot[rc] = rotations[rot_base + rc];
        int trans_base = (b * N + i) * 3;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) s_trans[c] = translations[trans_base + c];
    }
    __syncthreads();

    // Compute q_pts in global frame for this head
    if (lane == 0) {
        int qpts_base = ((b * N + i) * (h * Qp) + h_idx * Qp) * 3;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p) {
            #pragma unroll
            for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {
                float val = s_trans[c];
                int base = qpts_base + p * 3;
                #pragma unroll
                for (int c2 = 0; c2 < 3; ++c2) {
                    val += q_pts_local[base + c2] * s_rot[c2 * 3 + c];
                }
                s_qpts[p * 3 + c] = val;
            }
        }
    }
    __syncthreads();

    // softplus head weight (beta=1, threshold=20)
    float hw = head_weights[h_idx];
    float w = hw > 20.0f ? hw : log1pf(expf(hw));

    // load q scalar
    int q_base = ((b * N + i) * h + h_idx) * d;
    float q_vec[64];
    for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) q_vec[di] = q[q_base + di];

    float inv_sqrt_d = rsqrtf((float)d);

    // --- Pass 1: max logit over j ---
    float local_max = -1e30f;
    for (int j = lane; j < N; j += 32) {
        float dot = 0.0f;
        int k_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d;
        for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {
            dot += q_vec[di] * k[k_base + di];
        }
        float logit = dot * inv_sqrt_d;

        int kpts_base = ((b * N + j) * (h * Qp) + h_idx * Qp) * 3;
        int trans_j_base = (b * N + j) * 3;
        int rot_j_base = (b * N + j) * 9;
        float pt_dist = 0.0f;
        for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p) {
            for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {
                float kpt = translations[trans_j_base + c];
                int base = kpts_base + p * 3;
                for (int c2 = 0; c2 < 3; ++c2) {
                    kpt += k_pts_local[base + c2] * rotations[rot_j_base + c2 * 3 + c];
                }
                float diff = s_qpts[p * 3 + c] - kpt;
                pt_dist += diff * diff;
            }
        }
        logit += -(w * pt_dist) * 0.5f;

        int pb_idx = ((b * N + i) * N + j) * h + h_idx;
        logit += pair_bias[pb_idx];

        local_max = fmaxf(local_max, logit);
    }
    #pragma unroll
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
        local_max = fmaxf(local_max, __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_max, offset));
    }
    float global_max = local_max;

    // --- Pass 2: local sum of exp(logit - global_max) ---
    float local_sum = 0.0f;
    for (int j = lane; j < N; j += 32) {
        float dot = 0.0f;
        int k_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d;
        for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {
            dot += q_vec[di] * k[k_base + di];
        }
        float logit = dot * inv_sqrt_d;

        int kpts_base = ((b * N + j) * (h * Qp) + h_idx * Qp) * 3;
        int trans_j_base = (b * N + j) * 3;
        int rot_j_base = (b * N + j) * 9;
        float pt_dist = 0.0f;
        for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p) {
            for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {
                float kpt = translations[trans_j_base + c];
                int base = kpts_base + p * 3;
                for (int c2 = 0; c2 < 3; ++c2) {
                    kpt += k_pts_local[base + c2] * rotations[rot_j_base + c2 * 3 + c];
                }
                float diff = s_qpts[p * 3 + c] - kpt;
                pt_dist += diff * diff;
            }
        }
        logit += -(w * pt_dist) * 0.5f;

        int pb_idx = ((b * N + i) * N + j) * h + h_idx;
        logit += pair_bias[pb_idx];

        local_sum += expf(logit - global_max);
    }
    #pragma unroll
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
        local_sum += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum, offset);
    }
    float global_sum = local_sum;

    // --- Pass 3: aggregate weighted values ---
    float acc_scalar[64];
    for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) acc_scalar[di] = 0.0f;
    float acc_pt[24];
    for (int p = 0; p < Vp * 3; ++p) acc_pt[p] = 0.0f;

    for (int j = lane; j < N; j += 32) {
        float dot = 0.0f;
        int k_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d;
        for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {
            dot += q_vec[di] * k[k_base + di];
        }
        float logit = dot * inv_sqrt_d;

        int kpts_base = ((b * N + j) * (h * Qp) + h_idx * Qp) * 3;
        int trans_j_base = (b * N + j) * 3;
        int rot_j_base = (b * N + j) * 9;
        float pt_dist = 0.0f;
        for (int p = 0; p < Qp; ++p) {
            for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {
                float kpt = translations[trans_j_base + c];
                int base = kpts_base + p * 3;
                for (int c2 = 0; c2 < 3; ++c2) {
                    kpt += k_pts_local[base + c2] * rotations[rot_j_base + c2 * 3 + c];
                }
                float diff = s_qpts[p * 3 + c] - kpt;
                pt_dist += diff * diff;
            }
        }
        logit += -(w * pt_dist) * 0.5f;

        int pb_idx = ((b * N + i) * N + j) * h + h_idx;
        logit += pair_bias[pb_idx];

        float attn = expf(logit - global_max) / global_sum;

        int v_base = ((b * N + j) * h + h_idx) * d;
        for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {
            acc_scalar[di] += attn * v[v_base + di];
        }

        int vpts_base = ((b * N + j) * (h * Vp) + h_idx * Vp) * 3;
        for (int p = 0; p < Vp; ++p) {
            for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {
                float vpt = translations[trans_j_base + c];
                int base = vpts_base + p * 3;
                for (int c2 = 0; c2 < 3; ++c2) {
                    vpt += v_pts_local[base + c2] * rotations[rot_j_base + c2 * 3 + c];
                }
                acc_pt[p * 3 + c] += attn * vpt;
            }
        }
    }

    // warp-reduce accumulators
    for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {
        float val = acc_scalar[di];
        #pragma unroll
        for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
            val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset);
        }
        acc_scalar[di] = val;
    }
    for (int p = 0; p < Vp * 3; ++p) {
        float val = acc_pt[p];
        #pragma unroll
        for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
            val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset);
        }
        acc_pt[p] = val;
    }

    // lane 0 writes output
    if (lane == 0) {
        int out_base = (b * N + i) * (h * d + h * Vp * 3);
        for (int di = 0; di < d; ++di) {
            out[out_base + h_idx * d + di] = acc_scalar[di];
        }
        for (int p = 0; p < Vp; ++p) {
            float gpt[3];
            for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) gpt[c] = acc_pt[p * 3 + c];
            for (int d_out = 0; d_out < 3; ++d_out) {
                float local_val = 0.0f;
                for (int c = 0; c < 3; ++c) {
                    local_val += (gpt[c] - s_trans[c]) * s_rot[d_out * 3 + c];
                }
                out[out_base + h * d + h_idx * Vp * 3 + p * 3 + d_out] = local_val;
            }
        }
    }
}

torch::Tensor ipa_forward_cuda(
    torch::Tensor q,
    torch::Tensor k,
    torch::Tensor v,
    torch::Tensor q_pts_local,
    torch::Tensor k_pts_local,
    torch::Tensor v_pts_local,
    torch::Tensor pair_bias,
    torch::Tensor rotations,
    torch::Tensor translations,
    torch::Tensor head_weights) {

    int B = q.size(0);
    int N = q.size(1);
    int h = q.size(2);
    int d = q.size(3);
    int Qp = k_pts_local.size(2) / h;
    int Vp = v_pts_local.size(2) / h;

    int out_features = h * d + h * Vp * 3;
    auto out = torch::zeros({B, N, out_features}, q.options());

    int total_blocks = B * N * h;
    size_t shared_mem = sizeof(float) * (Qp * 3 + 9 + 3);

    ipa_forward_kernel<<<total_blocks, 32, shared_mem>>>(
        q.data_ptr<float>(),
        k.data_ptr<float>(),
        v.data_ptr<float>(),
        q_pts_local.data_ptr<float>(),
        k_pts_local.data_ptr<float>(),
        v_pts_local.data_ptr<float>(),
        pair_bias.data_ptr<float>(),
        rotations.data_ptr<float>(),
        translations.data_ptr<float>(),
        head_weights.data_ptr<float>(),
        out.data_ptr<float>(),
        B, N, h, d, Qp, Vp
    );

    return out;
}
'''

_C = load_inline(
    name="ipa_fused_v3",
    cpp_sources="torch::Tensor ipa_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor, torch::Tensor);",
    cuda_sources=cuda_source,
    functions=["ipa_forward_cuda"],
    extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"],
    verbose=False,
)


class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, node_dim, pair_dim, num_heads, num_query_points, num_value_points):
        super().__init__()
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.head_dim = node_dim // num_heads
        self.num_query_points = num_query_points
        self.num_value_points = num_value_points
        assert node_dim % num_heads == 0

        d = self.head_dim
        self.q_proj = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * d, bias=False)
        self.k_proj = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * d, bias=False)
        self.v_proj = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * d, bias=False)

        self.q_pts = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * num_query_points * 3, bias=False)
        self.k_pts = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * num_query_points * 3, bias=False)
        self.v_pts = nn.Linear(node_dim, num_heads * num_value_points * 3, bias=False)

        self.pair_bias = nn.Linear(pair_dim, num_heads, bias=False)

        self.head_weights = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(num_heads))

        out_features = num_heads * d + num_heads * num_value_points * 3
        self.out_proj = nn.Linear(out_features, node_dim)

        self.layer_norm = nn.LayerNorm(node_dim)

    def forward(
        self,
        node_repr: torch.Tensor,
        pair_repr: torch.Tensor,
        translations: torch.Tensor,
        rotations: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        B, N, D = node_repr.shape
        h = self.num_heads
        d = self.head_dim
        Qp = self.num_query_points
        Vp = self.num_value_points

        x = self.layer_norm(node_repr)

        q = self.q_proj(x).view(B, N, h, d)
        k = self.k_proj(x).view(B, N, h, d)
        v = self.v_proj(x).view(B, N, h, d)

        q_pts_local = self.q_pts(x).view(B, N, h * Qp, 3)
        k_pts_local = self.k_pts(x).view(B, N, h * Qp, 3)
        v_pts_local = self.v_pts(x).view(B, N, h * Vp, 3)

        pair_bias = self.pair_bias(pair_repr)  # (B, N, N, h)

        out = _C.ipa_forward_cuda(
            q.contiguous(),
            k.contiguous(),
            v.contiguous(),
            q_pts_local.contiguous(),
            k_pts_local.contiguous(),
            v_pts_local.contiguous(),
            pair_bias.contiguous(),
            rotations.contiguous(),
            translations.contiguous(),
            self.head_weights.contiguous(),
        )
        return self.out_proj(out)
